TITLE      Proton-induced production of residual radionuclides    O0500  1    3 
           in lead at intermediate energies                       O0500  1    4 
AUTHOR     (M.Gloris, R.Michel, F.Sudbrok, U.Herpers,             O0500  1    5 
           P.Malmborg, B.Holmqvist)                               O0500  1    6 
INSTITUTE  (2GERUH,2GERKLN,2SWDUPP)                               O0500  1    7 
REFERENCE  (J,NIM/A,463,593,2001)                                 O0500  1    8 
           (T,GLORIS,1998) - prelim. data tables. Dr.thesis       O0500  1    9 
            submitted to Uni. Hannover in 1998                    O0500  1   10 
REL-REF    (R,,U.Reus+,J,AND,29,1,1983) Decay-data.               O0500  1   11 
FACILITY   (SYNCY,2FR SAC) LNS - five experiments each consisting O0500  1   12 
           of two individual irradiations with different initial  O0500  1   13 
           proton energies above 200 MeV                          O0500  1   14 
           (CYCLO,2SWDUPP) TSL - Three irradiation experiments    O0500  1   15 
           were performed at the TSL during each of which three toO0500  1   16 
           to four different stacks were irradiated separately    O0500  1   17 
           at energies below 180 MeV                              O0500  1   18 
SAMPLE     Up to 30 small stacks from high-purity materials with  O0500  1   19 
           diam. of 15.0 mm were 55 or 125 mg/cm**2 for lead      O0500  1   20 
            (99.99% purity) and 10 or 33 mg/cm**2 for aluminum    O0500  1   21 
            (99.999% purity). In general, each unit consisted of  O0500  1   22 
           three aluminum foils and three to seven lead foils.    O0500  1   23 
           Only one or more of the inner Al respectively Pb foils O0500  1   24 
           were used for the measurements to avoid cross          O0500  1   25 
           contamination and recoil effects.                      O0500  1   26 
MONITOR    (13-AL-27(P,X)11-NA-22,CUM,SIG)                        O0500  1   27 
DECAY-DATA (11-NA-22,,DG,1274.5,0.999)                            O0500  1   28 
MONIT-REF  (O0276011,R.Michel+,J,NIM/B,129,153,1997)              O0500  1   29 
DETECTOR   (HPGE,GELI) Several high purity germanium and          O0500  1   30 
           germanium-lithium detectors partially equipped         O0500  1   31 
           with automatic sample changers were used. Typical      O0500  1   32 
           resolutions ranged from about 1 keV at 122 keV of Co-57O0500  1   33 
           to about 2 keV at 1332 keV of Co-60.                   O0500  1   34 
METHOD     (ACTIV,EXTB,BCINT,STTA)                                O0500  1   35 
           The irradiations were performed in air and lasted      O0500  1   36 
           typically about twelve hours to get sufficient fluence.O0500  1   37 
           support. For details of the experimental setup and     O0500  1   38 
           parameters of the experiments at LNS see Table 1 of    O0500  1   39 
           Nucl.Instr.Meth.,A463(2001)593                         O0500  1   40 
           (GSPEC) After end of irradiations the targets were     O0500  1   41 
           transported to Cologne were the stacks and mini-stacks O0500  1   42 
           were dismounted and the individual targets were        O0500  1   43 
           separated.  A part of them stayed at Cologne for       O0500  1   44 
           measurement, another one was transported to Hannover   O0500  1   45 
           for the same purpose. The gamma-spectrometric          O0500  1   46 
           measurements started about between 36 and 60 hours     O0500  1   47 
           after the end of irradiation, respectively.            O0500  1   48 
           Up to 30 measurements were made of each lead target    O0500  1   49 
           during a time span of up to two years after irradiationO0500  1   50 
           During this time each sample was measured on a minimum O0500  1   51 
           of five different detectors by this way avoiding       O0500  1   52 
           systematic errors. Measurement times ranged from five  O0500  1   53 
           minutes in the beginning up to about three days in     O0500  1   54 
           some cases at the end of a measurement series.         O0500  1   55 
            In some cases where we irradiated more than three leadO0500  1   56 
           targets at one energy point two adjacent targets were  O0500  1   57 
           measured together to get better counting statistics.   O0500  1   58 
ANALYSIS   (DECAY)                                                O0500  1   59 
ERR-ANALYS (ERR-T) Total uncertainty includes:                    O0500  1   60 
             * Uncertainties due to fluctuations in the beam      O0500  1   61 
            intensity become negligible.                          O0500  1   62 
           (ERR-8,,10.) Uncertainty of absorption of gamma-quanta O0500  1   63 
            in the sample                                         O0500  1   64 
             * Uncertainty of irradiation time, decay time and    O0500  1   65 
           counting time are negligible.                          O0500  1   66 
             * Uncertainty of impurities - due to the high purity O0500  1   67 
           of the target foils contributions of other constituentsO0500  1   68 
           were not considered.                                   O0500  1   69 
             * Uncertainty of nuclide production by secondary     O0500  1   70 
           particles                                              O0500  1   71 
             * The dead-time of the detector systems was          O0500  1   72 
           automatically corrected                                O0500  1   73 
           (ERR-1,,2.) uncertainty of the determination of net    O0500  1   74 
                       peak areas                                 O0500  1   75 
           (ERR-2) uncertainty of half-lives                      O0500  1   76 
           (ERR-3) Uncertainty of gamma-abundances -              O0500  1   77 
           abundances were also taken from REL-REF.               O0500  1   78 
           (ERR-4) Uncertainty of the full-energy-peak efficiency O0500  1   79 
           (ERR-5,,1.) Uncertainty of number of irradiated nuclei O0500  1   80 
           (ERR-6) Uncertainty of flux density                    O0500  1   81 
                 No uncertainties were attributed to the monitor  O0500  1   82 
           cross sections.                                        O0500  1   83 
           (ERR-7,,5.) uncertainty due to gamma-gamma-coincidencesO0500  1   84 
           in case of coincident gamma-rays < 5%.                 O0500  1   85 
CORRECTION While absorption of gamma-quanta in the aluminum       O0500  1   86 
           catcher foils played no role, it did in the lead foils.O0500  1   87 
           Since we evaluated our spectra for energies down to    O0500  1   88 
           95 keV we had to apply corrections for this effect.    O0500  1   89 
MISC-COL   (MISC1) Time of irradiation.                           O0500  1   90 
           (MISC2) Number of determinations.                      O0500  1   91 
COMMENT    -By authors- A cross section for the production of a   O0500  1   92 
           nuclide is denoted as independent if the nuclide can   O0500  1   93 
           only be produced directly via the nuclear reaction     O0500  1   94 
           between the projectile and the target nucleus and not  O0500  1   95 
           via subsequent beta-,beta+,EC- or alpha- decays. Such  O0500  1   96 
           independent cross sections are obtained if:            O0500  1   97 
            * either the nuclide is shielded by stable nucleus    O0500  1   98 
           against beta-decay or by a long-lived progenitor,      O0500  1   99 
            * or the cross section for the production of a        O0500  1  100 
           progenitor is also measured so that the production via O0500  1  101 
           decay can be corrected for.                            O0500  1  102
